  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1c45e10f-3142-4e5d-ab2d-cf34e62dd558'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1133052-do-you-have-to-have-read-the-first-books">Do you have to have read the first books of Shannara to understand this trilogy?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1133052'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F34988.The_Scions_of_Shannara">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1133052-do-you-have-to-have-read-the-first-books">3 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1133052-do-you-have-to-have-read-the-first-books">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/186483-beau"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1503856404i/186483._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/186483-beau">Beau</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Not necessarily, but you will get more out of this book if you read the original trilogy first (The Sword of Shannara, The Elfstones of Shannara, and <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Not necessarily, but you will get more out of this book if you read the original trilogy first (The Sword of Shannara, The Elfstones of Shannara, and The Wishsong of Shannara). There are many references to things that took place in those books. But still, the plot here should make sense, and I find this book better and more interesting than the original trilogy.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_661330372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/661330372" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/661330372?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661330372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11746226969981036283">I need a way to rate the book and then a way to separately rate the edition I got. I have the audio I got from OverDrive and the gain is so low that with the recording turned up all the way, my speakers turned up all the way and going into my computers audio controls and jacking them up all the way I could barely hear it. Recording value -1 star.<br/><br/>The book is a return to the world of the original Shannara trilogy though much later. magic is outlawed and practically gone (funny how often that seems</span>
  <span id="freeText11746226969981036283" style="display:none">I need a way to rate the book and then a way to separately rate the edition I got. I have the audio I got from OverDrive and the gain is so low that with the recording turned up all the way, my speakers turned up all the way and going into my computers audio controls and jacking them up all the way I could barely hear it. Recording value -1 star.<br /><br />The book is a return to the world of the original Shannara trilogy though much later. magic is outlawed and practically gone (funny how often that seems to happen in "fantasy worlds") Our hero(es) are tasked with saving the world, by bringing magic back, by finding the Sword of Shannara. (Hey just because that's how this whole series started don't knock it. When you get a good plot idea [or find a good plot idea] like "recovering a magic sword" use it as often as possible....right?)<br /><br />Anyway, did you get that? It's sort of a multilevel quest. They have to bring back magic to save the world, but they have to find the Sword of Shannara to bring back magic. Well, to find the truth about magic and saving the world.<br /><br />Now if you find that a bit convoluted, "shame on you how dare you criticize a classic work of fantasy"? At least that's the reaction I tend to get when i express opinions like that.<br /><br />Go figure.<br /><br />And by the way...someone's pretty ungrateful as there was already a quest to find the Sword of Shannara and when it was found someone obviously didn't take care of it, AND it seems they've lost the Elf Stones to!!!!<br /><br />We just can't have nice things....<br /><br />Not a bad book. If you get the audio I got, good luck on actually being able to hear it however. <br /><br /><br />*Just had to correct a word. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11746226969981036283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer372902337312948891">This was much better than I expected. I read the previous Shanara trilogy years ago and I remember thinking the first novel was a total Lord of the Rings ripoff. The second two were better but still followed the same structure of a quest to find some magical item to defeat a magical enemy.<br/><br/>This first novel of a new series started out much the same. We meet Par Ohmesford, a descendant of the previous heroes, who is quickly told he needs to find the same sword from the first novel to defeat yet ano</span>
  <span id="freeText372902337312948891" style="display:none">This was much better than I expected. I read the previous Shanara trilogy years ago and I remember thinking the first novel was a total Lord of the Rings ripoff. The second two were better but still followed the same structure of a quest to find some magical item to defeat a magical enemy.<br /><br />This first novel of a new series started out much the same. We meet Par Ohmesford, a descendant of the previous heroes, who is quickly told he needs to find the same sword from the first novel to defeat yet another shadowy evil. He bands together a group of adventurers, ala Fellowship of the Ring and heads out to meet Gandalf... Sorry I mean Allanon. <br /><br />By about the halfway point this book started to grip me more than its predecessors. I mostly enjoyed hearing about Par's uncle, the grouchy Walker Boh who represented a different kind of hero than we have seen so far in this series. And refreshingly of all, it seems like the second book in this series will be a direct sequel so everything didnt get nicely wrapped up for a change.<br /><br />Onto the next one!<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7183764309862098258">my first terry brooks novel, and purely by chance. since then, i was hooked. don't care if people say that brooks was a hack compared to tolkien. i like both authors--they have their own writing styles, and both are very good in their art. <br/><br/>what is great about brooks and his shannara series is that every chapter is riveting. there were times when i really couldn't put the book down--i just wanted to gobble up every scene, every confrontation, every revelation. besides having fantastical character</span>
  <span id="freeText7183764309862098258" style="display:none">my first terry brooks novel, and purely by chance. since then, i was hooked. don't care if people say that brooks was a hack compared to tolkien. i like both authors--they have their own writing styles, and both are very good in their art. <br /><br />what is great about brooks and his shannara series is that every chapter is riveting. there were times when i really couldn't put the book down--i just wanted to gobble up every scene, every confrontation, every revelation. besides having fantastical characters, there's also humor, romance, and even serious emotional turmoil. plus, the way brooks describes his characters and the world around them is so textured and rich: one can feel the beat of the sun on the characters' faces, the merciless twists and turns of the forests that they traverse, the pounding adrenalin as they are pursued, even the despair and exhilaration that overcomes them at salient points of their journeys. surely only something a master storyteller could execute.<br /><br />i'll always be grateful that i discovered the shannara series thru the Scions--(well, after this novel, it was just romance between me and its other installments... ^_^ )</span>

<div id="review_838021479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/838021479" />
    <a title="MC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28164369-mc"><img alt="MC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483779945p2/28164369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/838021479?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MC" href="/user/show/28164369-mc">MC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6581842-the-scions-of-shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer838021479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5550418799889392953">For <i>The Sword of Shannara Trilogy</i>, author Terry Brooks wrote three separate, but loosely-connected tales. In <i>The Heritage of Shannara</i>, he tells one large, epic tale over the space of four books. It was quite a departure from the pattern of the previous stories, and, if the first book is any indication, this seems to have worked quite well for Brooks.<br/><br/>As the first book, <i>The Scions of Shannara</i>, opens, the world is a radically different place from the world that Brin and Jair Ohmsford inhabited at t</span>
  <span id="freeText5550418799889392953" style="display:none">For <i>The Sword of Shannara Trilogy</i>, author Terry Brooks wrote three separate, but loosely-connected tales. In <i>The Heritage of Shannara</i>, he tells one large, epic tale over the space of four books. It was quite a departure from the pattern of the previous stories, and, if the first book is any indication, this seems to have worked quite well for Brooks.<br /><br />As the first book, <i>The Scions of Shannara</i>, opens, the world is a radically different place from the world that Brin and Jair Ohmsford inhabited at the end of <i>The Wishsong of Shannara</i>. The Federation, which was once misguided, but still democratic, has become a repressive state that has completely taken over the Southlands through conquest, and has enslaved the Dwarfs, and seem to be intent on driving them to extinction. Magic is outlawed, the elves have disappeared, and a new breed of evil, called the Shadowen, has arisen. Their very presence is causing the Four Lands to sicken and die.<br /><br />Amidst this situation, the shade of the Druid Allanon enlists the help of former Druid Cogline to persuade the heirs of the Elven House of Shannara to come to the Hadeshorn, where his spirit rests, and hear his requests to them. He has tried to contact these folks before, in their dreams, and they will not respond. Par Ohmsford is afraid, Wren Ohmsford is ambivalent, and Walker Boh (an Ohmsford who took the name of one of his forebears) is outright hostile. All of them, even Par who is the most idealistic about the Druids, share a suspicion of Allanon due to his manipulations of their ancestors centuries ago during the Druid's lifetime.<br /><br />After much persuasion from Cogline, they eventually go to the Hadeshorn to hear Allanon's spirit talk to them. The shade shows them a horrific future in which the Shadowen rule the lands and the people are mindless cattle to be fed upon and tortured for the amusement of these demonic creatures. He then gives them their tasks – ones that seem impossible to fulfill. But if they don't accomplish these tasks, the land will be plunged into darkness forever.<br /><br />Terry Brooks really improved his skills as an author in the time between the publication of <i>The Sword of Shannara</i> and <i>Scions</i>. The plotting is tighter, the characterization is actually somewhat in-depth and not the somewhat shallow portrayal of the first book. I love <i>Sword</i>, but I have to be fair on pointing out the problems from which it suffered. Of course, the romantic subplots are still rather sloppily done, with the one in the current book only working because of the length of the time they two characters are mentioned as near each other being longer. Brooks isn't good at writing romances. His attempts could be listed under tvtropes.com's “Strangled by the Red String” index, in which characters are just paired off together with no believable build-up.<br /><br />For me the best part of <i>Scions</i> was that the characters were more believable. They didn't take up the mission with no qualms, but struggled with it. They have fears, doubts, and uncertainties. In short, they were characters that one can relate to. I appreciated this aspect.<br /><br />That is not to say that <i>Scions</i> was perfect. To be sure, it had it's problems. Mainly insomuch as that the story dragged in parts. And the explanation about how the Shadowen developed was understandable, but a bit sloppily explained. It's something that you have to think through to get, and have to depend on your knowledge gained from having read the previous trilogy, because it <i>certainly</i> isn't put all that clearly here.<br /><br />This was a terrific effort by Brooks, and I am already eagerly beginning the second book of the <i>Heritage</i> story, <i>The Druid of Shannara</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5550418799889392953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_322573927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322573927" />
    <a title="Mitali" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7065529-mitali"><img alt="Mitali" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460721630p2/7065529.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322573927?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitali" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitali" href="/user/show/7065529-mitali">Mitali</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345370747" href="/book/show/544554.The_Scions_of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7065529-mitali?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7065529-mitali?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7065529-mitali?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7065529-mitali?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322573927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11588325508945322889">I first read this book about 3-4 years ago, but it was apparently so forgettable that I couldn't remember a thing about it apart from the very bare bones of the plot. Even when I started skimming through it to remind myself of more details (so that I could read its sequels), I had almost no memory of most of the scenes or even important characters, so I finally decided to reread the whole damn thing. Perhaps it's an exercise in masochism to reread something that my mind didn't think was worth ho</span>
  <span id="freeText11588325508945322889" style="display:none">I first read this book about 3-4 years ago, but it was apparently so forgettable that I couldn't remember a thing about it apart from the very bare bones of the plot. Even when I started skimming through it to remind myself of more details (so that I could read its sequels), I had almost no memory of most of the scenes or even important characters, so I finally decided to reread the whole damn thing. Perhaps it's an exercise in masochism to reread something that my mind didn't think was worth holding on to for barely a few years - yet at the end of it, I was mildly surprised to find that the book is quite engaging. Sure, it's derivative and filled with every fantasy cliché in the book. Sure, the prose is often hilariously awful. Yet, somehow, it's not a bad book on the whole, and can often be interesting. <br />The basic story - though a fairly straightforward fantasy quest - is decent enough. Three of the Shannara descendants - Par Ohmsford, Walker Boh and Wren Ohmsford - are summoned by the shade of the Druid Allanon to carry out certain tasks. This table setting takes up half the book, since the stories of each of these three are spread out over the sequels. A little condensation would have helped the pacing considerably, especially the later parts of this book, which mostly follows Par's quest to retrieve the long-lost sword of Shannara. The number of scenes in which Par and his brother Coll hide out in dark sheds while waiting for an opportunity to go after the sword are extremely numerous and extremely boring, especially Par's indecision and second guessing over everything he does. The few scenes of action that punctuate these hideout scenes are pretty good, though.<br />One thing I detest thoroughly is Brooks's tendency to constantly refer to characters by their geographical origin/race/occupation/etc. It's one thing when others in the rag-tag bunch of misfits, who may not know Par and Coll very well, refer to them both as 'Valemen'. But when the author himself keeps doing it constantly - even in scenes where no other characters are present - it gets extremely irritating. Ditto with his tendency to refer to Morgan as 'The Highlander' or Walker Boh as 'Dark Uncle' and so on. <br />Speaking of Walker Boh - after rereading 'Scions of Shannara', I realized why I had quit the sequel 'Druid of Shannara' halfway: because of how extremely annoying Boh is (he's the main character in the latter). His angst is too ridiculous for words, especially because the 'dark past' he is supposed to have seems to amount to nothing more than 'They don't like me because I'm DIFFERENT!' Most of the time, he seems like a whiny teenager rather than an adult haunted by a grim past. A little more fleshing out of his background would have done wonders for the character. It might also have explained how he is directly descended from Brin Ohmsford (of Wishsong of Shannara fame), while Par and Coll are not, even though he's their uncle by blood.<br />I could nitpick this book to death, but I'll stop now, because the bottomline is that despite the many flaws in this book, it remains mostly entertaining and a good ‘airplane read' (or in my case, a 'train read' for my daily commute). It's the kind of book in which if you think too hard about anything, it all falls apart. But if you let yourself get lost in the story, it can be quite enjoyable - so much so, that I feel motivated enough to read the second book again, Walker Boh be damned!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11588325508945322889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_523017296" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/523017296" />
    <a title="Shannan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5855666-shannan"><img alt="Shannan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342655015p2/5855666.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/523017296?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannan" href="/user/show/5855666-shannan">Shannan</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer523017296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7005273037203425106">I've been a fan of the various Shannara series' for a number of years but the Heritage series is probably my favourite. The brotherly bond with struggle and love is so well written that I really relate to Par and Coll. This is, in some ways, your standard sort of "epic fantasy" with elves, dwarves, humans, etc. but the personal stories carry it so much further than just any "standard" fantasy. I've read this series before, and I'll read it again! Love it.</span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18484922-dark-draco?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18484922-dark-draco?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer712922752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer397642752349336106">This is the first book in the second series of Shannara books. 300 years have passed since Brin destroyed the Ildatch, but the Four Lands are in turmoil. The Federation have begun to take over, enslaving the dwarves, fighting the trolls and banning magic. The elves have disappeared and dark Shadowen take over the bodies of the people they destroy. The shade of Allanon sends dreams to the three Ohmsford chidlren. Par has the power of the wishsong and is ordered to seek out the legendary Sword of </span>
  <span id="freeText397642752349336106" style="display:none">This is the first book in the second series of Shannara books. 300 years have passed since Brin destroyed the Ildatch, but the Four Lands are in turmoil. The Federation have begun to take over, enslaving the dwarves, fighting the trolls and banning magic. The elves have disappeared and dark Shadowen take over the bodies of the people they destroy. The shade of Allanon sends dreams to the three Ohmsford chidlren. Par has the power of the wishsong and is ordered to seek out the legendary Sword of Shannars. Walker Boh has to restore Paranor and the Druids, while Wren Ohmsford has to bring back the Elves. Each is reluctant to do so, but each is drawn to their quest.<br /><br />The main story follows Par, although occassionally shoots off to the other stories. Par and his brother, plus Morgan Leah, meet up with the outlaw, Padishar Creel, who thinks he knows where the Sword is hidden. But when they attempt to take it, they discover that the Federation has been hiding something nasty. And Par has to face the worst kind off truth.<br /><br />Another fantastic book in the series. Action-packed, fast-paced, you just keep on reading from cover to cover...and want to reach for the next without taking a breath. Some of the themes have been done to death in the previous books and the identity of the traitor in their midst is a bit obvious, but you can overlook the minor faults in the rest of the brilliance! Definitely one of my favourite fantasy epics.</span>
  <a data-text-id="397642752349336106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1497545702" />
    <a title="Roman Kurys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48577145-roman-kurys"><img alt="Roman Kurys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591566555p2/48577145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1497545702?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roman Kurys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roman Kurys" href="/user/show/48577145-roman-kurys">Roman Kurys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1497545702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7286824088594791699">So while I though the first Trilogy good, this has been GREAT! A fantastic ride through a good adventure courtesy of Terry Brooks. <br/><br/>I really love how he continually brings up events from the last 3 books in a non invasive manner that flows well with the story and also at the same time serves as a reminder of the times in the past. This has made it much easier to get immersed in the story and plenty of times I found hours slip by unnoticed and had to make myself stop reading to go on about my day.</span>
  <span id="freeText7286824088594791699" style="display:none">So while I though the first Trilogy good, this has been GREAT! A fantastic ride through a good adventure courtesy of Terry Brooks. <br /><br />I really love how he continually brings up events from the last 3 books in a non invasive manner that flows well with the story and also at the same time serves as a reminder of the times in the past. This has made it much easier to get immersed in the story and plenty of times I found hours slip by unnoticed and had to make myself stop reading to go on about my day.<br /><br />This books continues in the manner that made the previous trilogy great. If you're looking for deep political intrigues of Dune or lots of backstabbing ways of the Song of Fire and Ice, this series is not it.<br /><br />However, if you're looking for a good adventure with plenty of unexpected turns in plot and just pure raw Essence of an adventure, this right here, is worth the time.<br /><br />I learned to appreciate Brooks' ability to entwined descriptions, thoughts of characters and dialogue into a seemless story telling that is very immersive and at the same time does t require a dictionary every 5 pages.<br /><br />If you like fantasy genre, this is definitely a great read, and I'll definitely be reading the next part in my future reading adventures ;)<br /><br />Roman "Ragnar" <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7286824088594791699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16023658224634078469">I read this in hardcover the week it was released in 1990 and this was my first re-read.<br/><br/>The first Shannara trilogy were each stand alone stories and this one was the first series where the "story" spanned multiple volumes (in this case four books) so this was definitely a different feel from Brooks earlier works.<br/><br/>Gotta tell you - I really liked this book, liked it the first time I read it and liked it this time.<br/><br/>It had great characters that evolved and developed as the story moved. It had great pl</span>
  <span id="freeText16023658224634078469" style="display:none">I read this in hardcover the week it was released in 1990 and this was my first re-read.<br /><br />The first Shannara trilogy were each stand alone stories and this one was the first series where the "story" spanned multiple volumes (in this case four books) so this was definitely a different feel from Brooks earlier works.<br /><br />Gotta tell you - I really liked this book, liked it the first time I read it and liked it this time.<br /><br />It had great characters that evolved and developed as the story moved. It had great plotting - tight, fast moving with well developed cliff hangers. I cared about the characters and was invested in the story. <br /><br />We have the shade of Allanon coming back with a few demands....<br />Par must find the Sword of Shannara<br />Wren must find and bring back the elves<br />Walker Boh must bring back Paranor and the Druids<br />Or else the Shadowen win and the world as we know it is destroyed<br /><br />Good stuff - looking forward to continuing my re-read of this series.</span>

  <span id="freeText13661754818877522243" style="display:none">Oof, I accidentally deleted my original review from 2016. Well done, Goodreads app! Remind me to log on the computer next time, haha.<br /><br />Thanks to the virus lock down I have all this extra time to read - I can say I am a bit excited about this, haha.<br /><br />Loved this installment, and some parts still surprised me, even though this is a reread. This is again a Terry Brooks story, so there are many parallels with the other books. Think of the storyline and the characters, there is a set pattern in these books. I'm not really annoyed by it, but I can imagine some people are. I love that this story spans multiple books, the first books were really one story a book. <div id="review_3196682534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3196682534" />
    <a title="Brittney Tyler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56506626-brittney-tyler"><img alt="Brittney Tyler" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3196682534?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney Tyler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney Tyler" href="/user/show/56506626-brittney-tyler">Brittney Tyler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345370747" href="/book/show/544554.The_Scions_of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!!!!!!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56506626-brittney-tyler?shelf=dream-personal-library">dream-personal-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3196682534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12321240137416237492">Star Rating: 5 stars<br/><br/>Note: This is the 1st book in the Heritage of Shannara series but the 4th book in the overarching Shannara series so this will not be an in-depth review. <br/><br/>To keep up my steady progress of reading all the Shannara books by Terry Brooks in the proper order,decided to pick up The Scions of Shannara, which is book 1 of the Heritage of Shannara series but book 4 in the overarching Shannara saga. This book is set about 300 years after the events of book 3, The WishSong of Shannara t</span>
  <span id="freeText12321240137416237492" style="display:none">Star Rating: 5 stars<br /><br />Note: This is the 1st book in the Heritage of Shannara series but the 4th book in the overarching Shannara series so this will not be an in-depth review. <br /><br />To keep up my steady progress of reading all the Shannara books by Terry Brooks in the proper order,decided to pick up The Scions of Shannara, which is book 1 of the Heritage of Shannara series but book 4 in the overarching Shannara saga. This book is set about 300 years after the events of book 3, The WishSong of Shannara take place, and the world of the Four Lands has need of the Ohmsford family again. A totalitarian system call the Federation is slowly spreading their control across the Four Lands. Magic has been outlawed, the Elves have disappeared, the Dwarves are being used as slaves, and the Trolls have retreated deep into the Northland to avoid persecution. If all that wasn’t bad enough, a new dark evil has taken root in the land in the form of Shadowen. Can the Ohmsfords, along with their friends from some other well-known families- the Leahs and the Creels for instance- stop the dark progression of the Four Lands and keep it from reverting back to the habits that caused their near-total annihilation in the distant past. (If you read book 1, The Sword of Shannara, then you will understand where this allusion comes from.)<br /><br />My favorite part of this book is the characters as on one hand they are the traditional archetypes that we see in a lot of classic, epic fantasy, which makes them familiar, but they are also unique in their own ways. Brooks loves to create vast casts of characters and pit them against each other to create juxtaposition and growth/developments. One of his favorite relationships to explore is the sibling relationship as all of his books so far have at least one set of siblings in them. If characters that adhere to classic motifs but still allow for unique growth is your thing, then this book is for you. <br /><br />Speaking of motifs, this book/series is full of them as we explore what talismans, heritage, and power mean to people, societies, and the world as a whole. This book/series digs deep into the concept of how heritage can affect a society, especially when it is taken away and how the talismans that represent that heritage can become beacons of hope and empower a people to stand up and fight back against the ones that would destroy that heritage. I can’t wait to see how Brooks develops this idea in the other books within this quartet and across this epic series as a whole. <br /><br />All in all, this is my all-time favorite series by my all-time favorite author, and I know it won’t be everybody’s cup of tea, but it is definitely mine! 5 stars as always!!!!! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12321240137416237492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1548789223?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Squire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Squire" href="/user/show/15986821-squire">Squire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15986821-squire?shelf=2016-epic-shannara-quest">2016-epic-shannara-quest</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1548789223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer797243458583931301">#14/29 in my Epic Shannara Quest.<br/><br/>Three-hundred years after his death, the druid Allanon is at it again, calling upon the descendants of the Elven house of Shannara to stamp out evil threatening the Four Lands. This time he has three of them to contend with, each with their own personalities and egos.<br/><br/><i>?"...There is a history that needs repeating. There are adventures to be shared and battles to be won. This is what Fate has decreed for you and me!"</i><br/><br/>This is the problem with the beginning of this new</span>
  <span id="freeText797243458583931301" style="display:none">#14/29 in my Epic Shannara Quest.<br /><br />Three-hundred years after his death, the druid Allanon is at it again, calling upon the descendants of the Elven house of Shannara to stamp out evil threatening the Four Lands. This time he has three of them to contend with, each with their own personalities and egos.<br /><br /><i>?"...There is a history that needs repeating. There are adventures to be shared and battles to be won. This is what Fate has decreed for you and me!"</i><br /><br />This is the problem with the beginning of this new series. Brooks is repeating himself, conveniently giving himself a main protagonist who is a bard of sorts and keeps his family's heritage alive by telling stories of the events of the original Shannara trilogy, amplified by the wishsong (he is constantly recalling information from his stories for the benefit of newcomers to the world of Shannara). The reader also crosses paths with Padishar Creel, the great, great. great--ad naseum--grandson of Pannamon Creel from <i>The Sword of Shannara</i>.<br /><br />But repetition aside, Brooks' story here is strong and once he gets to the city of Tyrsis, and we get to see how the city has changed over the last 400 years, <i>The Scions of Shannara</i> becomes it's own creature. Full of colorful characters and sequences that are wonderfully imaginative and exciting, Brooks is also showing his development as a writer--he is starting to employ an economy of language that gives his story a momentum not found in his previous Shannara works (to this point, only the original trilogy, which were pretty dense linguistically). <br /><br />Overall, a fine, entertaining read.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="797243458583931301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138157603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1194706658044169734">I am a longtime Terry Brooks fan but have primarily focused on his Magic Kingdom and Word and the Void stories. So I haven't yet completed all of the Shannara books and decided it was time to do so. This book is the first I've read since Wishsong. Wishsong wasn't my favorite Brooks book, so I wasn't sure how much I would like this one. I am happy to report that I really enjoyed this story and the characters. It was interesting to see what Brooks had done with the world and the battle sequences w</span>
  <span id="freeText1194706658044169734" style="display:none">I am a longtime Terry Brooks fan but have primarily focused on his Magic Kingdom and Word and the Void stories. So I haven't yet completed all of the Shannara books and decided it was time to do so. This book is the first I've read since Wishsong. Wishsong wasn't my favorite Brooks book, so I wasn't sure how much I would like this one. I am happy to report that I really enjoyed this story and the characters. It was interesting to see what Brooks had done with the world and the battle sequences were top notch. It felt a little forced in a few places--where characters were sent to locations or into events more because it served the plot than through any organic need, but these problems were minor and, as a whole, the book was superior to both Sword and Wishsong. I recommend it to any Brooks or epic fantasy fan. I am excited to find out what happens next. </span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText12950067428424655471" style="display:none">Terry Brooks books are just so good! They are fast paced when they need to be - it's nice to have a lot of action! But, they also weave a deep story with lots of detail...which makes the 400+ pages just fly by.<br />This story continues building on the original Sword of Shannara series - bringing back the sword, the elfstones, the wishsong - the story is a similar adventure/quest to find the magical item and defeat the evil/magical demons. Which means lots of worldbuilding and magical action scenes. <br />The only thing I find slightly offputting about these books is that the main characters tend to whine about their magic more than they need to. Come on guys you have a magical powers - what could be cooler than that!?<br />Another great perk of this book is that I got it at a used store with the entire series for about $4 for all!         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81569130-stephanie-carr?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3311114846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17155026894148077569">3.5<br/><br/>It's much better than the first three books and all, and it's clearly going to be an actual, what, four books, that are all one story instead of fitting one story into one book. The characters have more depth, more -believable- depth, I should say. The plot is still mostly straight forward but it has its own little twists. <br/><br/>Twists that are all too often way too obvious. I almost gave this book 4 stars, but I just couldn't really push it that far just yet. I mean, the last little climax was so.</span>
  <span id="freeText17155026894148077569" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />It's much better than the first three books and all, and it's clearly going to be an actual, what, four books, that are all one story instead of fitting one story into one book. The characters have more depth, more -believable- depth, I should say. The plot is still mostly straight forward but it has its own little twists. <br /><br />Twists that are all too often way too obvious. I almost gave this book 4 stars, but I just couldn't really push it that far just yet. I mean, the last little climax was so. freakin. rushed. And then it barely pulls away from that rush to whoops, here's the ending. Like, not really the best ending as far as pacing. (Cause there's so much lead up and then, bloop lol). The try/fail sequences are fun though. <br /><br />Still. I liked it. Had enough power to pull me away from my gaming soooooo it's got that going for it. You can definitely tell Terry Brooks gets better with each book, which is kind of fun to notice in its own right. We're just not quite at 4 star "I really liked it" yet. (But we're close~)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17155026894148077569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

I took me a little to adjust to the new characters but I feel like not that much has changed. They are still a story of two bothers. Although one is now an elf, I small thing to look over. <div id="review_2202397778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2202397778" />
    <a title="NathanDoussot" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74532867-nathandoussot"><img alt="NathanDoussot" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2202397778?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NathanDoussot" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NathanDoussot" href="/user/show/74532867-nathandoussot">NathanDoussot</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2202397778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8453318587120863992">"The Scions of Shannara" is one of many books set in The Four Lands, which is populated by humans, elves, dwarves, trolls and other peoples. We mainly view this story from the viewpoint of 2 brothers, Par and Coll Omhsford. They journey through an oppressed land, where magic is outlawed and many non-humans are subjected under a totalitarian rule, all the while beings called shades propagate and seek to take over the land. They set out on a search for the Sword of Shannara, which has been lost fo</span>
  <span id="freeText8453318587120863992" style="display:none">"The Scions of Shannara" is one of many books set in The Four Lands, which is populated by humans, elves, dwarves, trolls and other peoples. We mainly view this story from the viewpoint of 2 brothers, Par and Coll Omhsford. They journey through an oppressed land, where magic is outlawed and many non-humans are subjected under a totalitarian rule, all the while beings called shades propagate and seek to take over the land. They set out on a search for the Sword of Shannara, which has been lost for generations, to prevent all life from being destroyed.<br /><br />In my opinion, this book was not that great. It has a Tolkien-esque world like a lot of other fantasy and I don't feel it distinguishes itself from the majority of the genre. The dialogue was awkward at times and I never really felt invested in the characters. At some points it really felt like a slog reading this. This is why I am giving it 2/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8453318587120863992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6elyAA/wwco07j/+Ws9dDrUZJe1c5+BkR9VBd6Kow9zruEzXsRZe1YubtHuSdq9diZ+G7F62/3D2f5qqj01ULw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

Ma alle 13 dal vicino Vesuvius si sprigiona una quantità di energia pari a cinquantamila bombe atomiche e, in meno di venti ore, sotto un diluvio ustionante di ceneri e gas, Pompei è soffocata da sei metri di pomici, mentre la vicina Ercolano viene sepolta sotto venti metri di fanghi compatti. Migliaia di uomini e donne cercano di scappare, invocano gli dèi, ma trovano una morte orribile. E solo in epoca moderna saranno scoperti alcuni dei loro corpi, contorti nella disperazione della fuga. Dopo molti anni passati a studiare la zona vesuviana, con il supporto di archeologi e vulcanologi Alberto Angela ricostruisce come in presa diretta i giorni che ne segnarono il tragico destino. Per farci respirare le atmosfere di quei momenti, individua alcuni personaggi storicamente esistiti – la ricca matrona Rectina, un cinico banchiere, un politico ambizioso… – e li segue passo dopo passo, in un percorso che si può fare ancora oggi, per strade, campagne, case o locali pubblici. In questo modo, non solo ci fa scorrere davanti agli occhi la vita quotidiana (prima) e la morte (poi) come in un film mozzafiato, ma dà anche nuove, illuminanti risposte a intriganti interrogativi: perché nessuno si era accorto di vivere alle pendici di un vulcano-killer? Come mai alcune eleganti domus erano diventate laboratori artigiani? E che cosa legava Plinio il Vecchio, naturalista e ammiraglio scomparso nella tragedia, all’affascinante Rectina? Dettagliatissimo e aggiornato con gli studi più recenti, è un viaggio emozionante nel mondo antico, lo sconvolgente reportage di una tragedia, un libro unico che si legge come un romanzo e ha la profondità di un grande saggio. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13000200558294589316">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word & Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his</span>
  <span id="freeText13000200558294589316" style="display:none">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word &amp; Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his graduate degree from the School of Law at Washington &amp; Lee University.<br />A writer since high school, he wrote many stories within the genres of science fiction, western, fiction, and non-fiction, until one semester early in his college years he was given The Lord of the Rings to read. That moment changed Terry's life forever, because in Tolkien's great work he found all the elements needed to fully explore his writing combined in one genre.<br />He then wrote The Sword of Shannara, the seven year grand result retaining sanity while studying at Washington &amp; Lee University and practicing law. It became the first work of fiction ever to appear on the New York Times trade paperback bestseller list, where it remained for over five months.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13000200558294589316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
